instance of an actual provider so it can return\n25: // the correct schema and validate the configuration accurately. func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n621: \t\t\t// We're only concerned with known null values, which can be computed\n622: \t\t\t// by the provider.\n623: \t\t\tif !v.IsKnown() {\n624: \t\t\t\treturn v, nil\n625: \t\t\t}\n626: \n627: \t\t\tattrSchema := schema.Body.AttributeByPath(path)\n628: \t\t\tif attrSchema == nil {\n629: \t\t\t\t// this is an intermediate path which does not represent an attribute\n630: \t\t\t\treturn v, nil\n631: \t\t\t}\n632: \n633: \t\t\t// Write-only attributes always return null\n634: \t\t\tif attrSchema.WriteOnly {\n635: \t\t\t\treturn \t\tresp.NewState = newVal\n644: \t} else {\n645: \t\tresp.NewState = r.PriorState\n646: \t}\n647: \n648: \tresp.Identity = r.CurrentIdentity\n649: \tresp.Private = r.Private\n650: \treturn resp\n651: }\n652: \n653: func (p *MockProvider) PlanResourceChange(r providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest) (resp providers.PlanResourceChangeResponse) {\n654: \tdefer p.beginWrite()()\n655: \n656: \tif !p.ConfigureProviderCalled {\n657: \t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"Configure not called before PlanResourceChange %q\", r.TypeName))\n658: \t\treturn resp\n659: \t}\n660: \n661: \tp.PlanResourceChangeCalled = true\n662: \tp.PlanResourceChangeRequest = r\n663: \n664: \tif p.PlanResourceChangeFn != nil {\n665: \t\treturn p.PlanResourceChangeFn(r)\n666: \t}\n667: \n668: \tif p.PlanResourceChangeResponse != nil {\n669: \t\treturn *p.PlanResourceChangeResponse\n670: \t}\n671: \n672: \t// this is a destroy plan,\n673: \tif r.ProposedNewState.IsNull() {\n674: \t\tresp.PlannedState = r.ProposedNewState\n675: \t\tresp.PlannedPrivate = r.PriorPrivate\n676: \t\treturn resp\n677: \t}\n678: \n679: \tschema, ok := p.getProviderSchema().ResourceTypes[r.TypeName]\n680: \tif !ok {\n681: \t\tresp.Diagnostics = resp.Diagnostics.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"no schema found for %q\", r.TypeName))\n682: \t\treturn resp\n683: \t}\n684: \n685: \t// The default plan behavior is to accept the proposed value, and mark all\n686: \t// nil computed attributes as unknown.\n687: \tval, err := cty.Transform(r.ProposedNewState, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n688: \t\t// We're only concerned with known null values, which can be computed\n689: \t\t// by the provider.\n690: \t\tif !v.IsKnown() {\n691: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n692: \t\t}\n693: \n694: \t\tattrSchema := schema.Body.AttributeByPath(path)\n695: \t\tif attrSchema == nil {\n696: \t\t\t// this is an intermediate path which does not represent an attribute\n697: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n698: \t\t}\n699: \n700: \t\t// Write-only attributes always return null\n701: \t\tif attrSchema.WriteOnly {\n702: \t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n703: \t\t}\n704: \n705: \t\t// get the current configuration value, to detect when a\n706: \t\t// computed+optional attributes has become unset\n707: \t\tconfigVal, err := path.Apply(r.Config)\n708: \t\tif err != nil {\n709: \t\t\t// cty can't currently apply some paths, so don't try to guess\n710: \t\t\t// what's needed here and return the proposed part of the value.\n711: \t\t\t// This is only a helper to create a default plan value, any tests\n712: \t\t\t// relying on specific plan behavior will create their own\n713: \t\t\t// PlanResourceChange responses.\n714: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n715: \t\t}\n716: \n717: \t\tswitch {\n718: \t\tcase attrSchema.Computed && !attrSchema.Optional && v.IsNull():\n719: \t\t\t// this is the easy path, this value is not yet set, and _must_ be computed\n720: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(v.Type()), nil\n721: \n722: \t\tcase attrSchema.Computed && attrSchema.Optional && !v.IsNull() && configVal.IsNull():\n723: \t\t\t// If an optional+computed value has gone from set to unset, it\n724: \t\t\t// becomes computed. (this was not possible to do with legacy\n725: \t\t\t// providers)\n726: \t\t\treturn cty.UnknownVal(v.Type()), nil\n727: \t\t}\n728: \n729: \t\treturn v, nil\n730: \t})\n731: \tif err != nil {\n732: In some cases, flattening and expanding need conditional handling.\n292: One important case is new AWS API implementations where the input or output structs make use of [union types](https://smithy.io/2.0/spec/aggregate-types.html#union).\n293: The AWS implementation uses an interface as the common type, along with various concrete implementations.\n294: Because the
